   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Google Pay</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Mobile payments platform developed by Google
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Google_Play" title="Google Play">Google Play</a>.
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For the peer-to-peer payments service from Google, see <a href="/wiki/Google_Pay_Send" title="Google Pay Send">Google Pay Send</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>Google Pay</b> (stylized as <b>G Pay</b>; formerly <b>Pay with Google</b> and <b>Android Pay</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Digital_wallet" title="Digital wallet">digital wallet</a> platform and <a href="/wiki/E-commerce_payment_system" title="E-commerce payment system">online payment</a> system developed by <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> to power in-app and tap-to-pay purchases on mobile devices, enabling users to make payments with <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> phones, tablets or <a href="/wiki/Smartwatch" title="Smartwatch">watches</a>. Users in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> can also use an iOS device, albeit with limited functionality. In addition to this, the service also supports passes such as coupons, boarding passes, student ID cards, event tickets, movie tickets, public transportation tickets, store cards, and loyalty cards. </p>
      <p>As of January 8, 2018, the old Android Pay and <a href="/wiki/Google_Wallet" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Wallet">Google Wallet</a> have unified into a single pay system called Google Pay.<sup id="cite_ref-Nieva_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nieva-3">[3]</a></sup> Android Pay was rebranded and renamed as Google Pay. It also took over the branding of <a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">Google Chrome</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Autofill" title="Autofill">autofill feature</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Google Pay adopts the features of both Android Pay and Google Wallet through its in-store, peer-to-peer, and online payments services.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nieva_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nieva-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The rebranded service provided a new <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" class="mw-redirect" title="Application programming interface">API</a> that allows merchants to add the payment service to websites, apps, <a href="/wiki/Stripe_(company)" title="Stripe (company)">Stripe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braintree_(company)" title="Braintree (company)">Braintree</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Google_Assistant" title="Google Assistant">Google Assistant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The service allows users to use the payment cards they have on file in their Google Account.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Service">Service</span></h2> 
      <p>Google Pay uses <a href="/wiki/Near-field_communication" title="Near-field communication">near-field communication</a> (NFC) to transmit card information facilitating funds transfer to the retailer. It replaces the <a href="/wiki/Credit_card" title="Credit card">credit</a> or <a href="/wiki/Debit_card" title="Debit card">debit</a> card <a href="/wiki/Chip_and_PIN" class="mw-redirect" title="Chip and PIN">chip and PIN</a> or <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_stripe_card" title="Magnetic stripe card">magnetic stripe</a> transaction at <a href="/wiki/Point-of-sale_terminal" class="mw-redirect" title="Point-of-sale terminal">point-of-sale terminals</a> by allowing the user to upload these in the Google Pay wallet. It is similar to contactless payments already used in many countries, with the addition of <a href="/wiki/Two-factor_authentication" class="mw-redirect" title="Two-factor authentication">two-factor authentication</a>. The service lets Android devices wirelessly communicate with <a href="/wiki/Point_of_sale" title="Point of sale">point of sale</a> systems using a <a href="/wiki/Near_field_communication" class="mw-redirect" title="Near field communication">near field communication</a> (NFC) antenna, <a href="/wiki/Host_card_emulation" title="Host card emulation">host-based card emulation (HCE)</a>, and Android's security. </p>
      <p>Google Pay takes advantage of physical authentications such as fingerprint ID where available. On devices without fingerprint ID, Google Pay is activated with a passcode. When the user makes a payment to a merchant, Google Pay does not send the credit or debit card number with the payment. Instead, it generates a virtual account number representing the user's account information. This service keeps customer payment information private, sending a one-time security code instead of the card or user details.<sup id="cite_ref-TheVerge-androidpay_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheVerge-androidpay-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Google Pay requires that a screen lock be set on the phone.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> It has no card limit.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Users can add payment cards to the service by taking a photo of the card, or by entering the card information manually. To pay at <a href="/wiki/Point_of_sale" title="Point of sale">points of sale</a>, users hold their authenticated device to the point of sale system. The service has smart-authentication, allowing the system to detect when the device is considered secure (for instance if unlocked in the last five minutes) and challenge if necessary for unlock information.<sup id="cite_ref-fingerp15_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fingerp15-13">[13]</a></sup> Spring CEO Alan Tisch said Google Pay improves mobile shopping business by supporting a "buy button" powered by Google Pay integrated within vendor's creative design.<sup id="cite_ref-TheVerge-androidpay2_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheVerge-androidpay2-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span></h3> 
      <p>Google Pay uses the EMV Payment Tokenisation Specification.<sup id="cite_ref-emvpaytok_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emvpaytok-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The service keeps customer payment information private from the retailer by replacing the customer's credit or debit card <a href="/wiki/Primary_Account_Number" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary Account Number">Funding Primary Account Number</a> (FPAN) with a tokenized Device Primary Account Number (DPAN), and creates a "dynamic security code [...] generated for each transaction". The 'dynamic security code' is the cryptogram in an <a href="/wiki/EMV" title="EMV">EMV</a>-mode transaction, and the Dynamic Card Verification Value (dCVV) in a magnetic stripe data emulation-mode transaction. Users can also remotely halt the service on a lost phone via Google's <a href="/wiki/Find_My_Device" title="Find My Device">Find My Device</a> service. </p>
      <p>To pay at points of sale, users hold their authenticated Android device to the point of sale system's NFC reader. Android users authenticate unlocking their phone by using biometrics, a pattern, or a passcode, whereas <a href="/wiki/Wear_OS" title="Wear OS">Wear OS</a> users authenticate by opening the app prior to payment.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> To pay in supported Android apps, users choose Google Pay as their payment method and authenticate with biometrics, a pattern, or a passcode. Users can add payment cards to the service in any of four ways: through the payment card listed on their Google accounts, by taking a photo of the card, being provisioned from within the card issuer's app, or by entering the card information manually. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Consumer_Device_Cardholder_Verification_Method_.28CDCVM.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumer_Device_Cardholder_Verification_Method_(CDCVM)">Consumer Device Cardholder Verification Method (CDCVM)</span></h3> 
      <p>In EMV-mode transactions, Google Pay supports the use of the Consumer Device Cardholder Verification Method (CDCVM) using biometrics, pattern, or the phone's or watch's passcode. The use of CDCVM allows for the device itself to provide verification for the transaction and may not require the cardholder to sign a receipt or enter their PIN. Additionally, in certain markets which have a 'no verification contactless limit' using contactless cards (such as the £45 limit in the United Kingdom and the C$100 limit in Canada), the use of CDCVM can enable merchants to accept transactions higher than these amounts using Google Pay, providing their terminal software is updated to support the latest network contactless specifications.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <p>Originally launched as Android Pay, the service was released at <a href="/wiki/Google_I/O" title="Google I/O">Google I/O</a> 2015. Android Pay was a successor to and built on the base established by <a href="/wiki/Google_Wallet" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Wallet">Google Wallet</a> which was released in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-WalletYT2011_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WalletYT2011-19">[19]</a></sup> It also used technology from the carrier-backed <a href="/wiki/Softcard" title="Softcard">Softcard</a>—Google had acquired its intellectual property in February 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-TheVerge-androidpay_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheVerge-androidpay-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TheVerge-Softshut_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheVerge-Softshut-20">[20]</a></sup> At launch, the service was compatible with 70% of Android devices, and was accepted at over 700,000 merchants.<sup id="cite_ref-TheVerge-androidpay_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheVerge-androidpay-8">[8]</a></sup> Google Wallet still powered web-based Play Store purchases and some app-based peer-to-peer payments, for instance in Gmail.<sup id="cite_ref-TheVerge-androidpay_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheVerge-androidpay-8">[8]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:138px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Android_Pay_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Android_Pay_logo.svg/136px-Android_Pay_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="136" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Android_Pay_logo.svg/204px-Android_Pay_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Android_Pay_logo.svg/272px-Android_Pay_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Android_Pay_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The logo of the former branding of the service, <i>Android Pay</i>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Google_Pay&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it is currently available in 40 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Upon its UK launch Android Pay supported MasterCard and Visa credit and debit cards from many of the UK's major financial institutions — including Bank of Scotland, First Direct, Halifax, HSBC, Lloyds Bank, M&amp;S Bank, MBNA and Nationwide Building Society — "with new banks being added all the time" according to Google. Natwest, RBS and Ulster Bank launched on September 14, 2016. On September 8, 2016 it was reported that UK banks TSB and Santander would be participating in the following weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Android Pay was launched in Singapore on June 28, 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and in Australia on July 14, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Android Pay launched in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> on December 7, 2016 and was initially available to customers of <a href="/wiki/Allied_Irish_Banks" title="Allied Irish Banks">AIB</a> and <a href="/wiki/KBC_Bank_Ireland" title="KBC Bank Ireland">KBC</a>, having since been extended to <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Ireland" title="Bank of Ireland">Bank of Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Bank" title="Ulster Bank">Ulster Bank</a>. The service works with both credit and debit cards.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2016, Google began a public trial in <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a> of a related <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">mobile app</a> called Hands Free. In this system, the customer does not need to present a phone or card. Instead, a customer announces they wish to "pay with Google" and give their initials to the cashier, who verifies their identity with a photo previously uploaded to the system. The customer's phone will only authorize payment if its geographic location system indicates it is near a participating store.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On September 18, 2017, Google launched an <a href="/wiki/Unified_Payments_Interface" title="Unified Payments Interface">UPI</a>-based app <a href="/wiki/Tez_(software)" title="Tez (software)">Tez</a> in India.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> On August 28, 2018, Google rebranded Tez to Google Pay.<sup id="cite_ref-tez-is-now-pay_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tez-is-now-pay-30">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On January 8, 2018, Google announced that <a href="/wiki/Google_Wallet" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Wallet">Google Wallet</a> would be merged into Android Pay, with the service as a whole rebranded as Google Pay.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> This merger extends the platform into web-based payments integrated into other Google and third-party services. The rebranding began to roll out as an update to the Android Pay app on February 20, 2018; the app was given an updated design, and now displays a personalized list of nearby stores which support Google Pay.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On December 21, 2018, Google Payment, obtained an e-money license in <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> - the license will enable Google to process payments, issue e-money, and handle electronic money wallets in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On November 17, 2020, Google Pay was made available in ten new European countries: Austria, Bulgaria, Estonia, Greece, Hungary, Latvia, Lithuania, Netherlands, Portugal, and Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Google Pay for these countries works without the app but as a service. The app won't be available for download as stated by Google in Google Pay Help page. <sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> On November 18, 2020, Google Pay was redesigned for the United States' version of the app, based upon the previous Indian/Singaporean versions of the app, which themselves were built upon Tez using the <a href="/wiki/Flutter_(software)" title="Flutter (software)">Flutter</a> codebase. This new app provides improved peer-to-peer payment functionality, deeper integration with businesses that are able to offer consumers offers and discounts for using the app, and more quality of life features such as searchable receipts.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecosystem">Ecosystem</span></h2> 
      <p>Google Pay has a passes feature, which exists in a larger ecosystem. They are presented in the bottom half of the app and can be sorted manually. Developers must first be granted access to the Google Pay API for Passes before they can author such items.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In its simplest form, an interaction (or transaction) between a pass and a system is facilitated by a 1D or 2D code, although it requires the customer to initiate the activity. Passes can also contain nothing but plain text or an image. </p>
      <p>More advanced passes would be ones that incorporate NFC technology to convey. <a href="/wiki/Walgreens" title="Walgreens">Walgreens</a> enabled this first with their Balance Rewards loyalty program in 2015; customers can add their card to Google Pay and be able to tap their phone to the terminal when prompted for their rewards card.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Since then, more businesses have found uses for these types of passes, like with contactless ticketing at <a href="/wiki/NCAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA">NCAA</a><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/MLB" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB">MLB</a> sports arenas<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Dave_%26_Buster%27s" title="Dave &amp; Buster's">Dave &amp; Buster's</a> Power Cards.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition to retailer-specific passes, Google Pay also supports contactless student IDs through the Transact eAccounts application, as well as transit tickets and passes such as the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Monorail" title="Las Vegas Monorail">Las Vegas Monorail</a> and Portland <a href="/wiki/Tri-Met" class="mw-redirect" title="Tri-Met">Tri-Met's</a> <a href="/wiki/Hop_Fastpass" title="Hop Fastpass">Hop Fastpass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Passes that can be transmitted through NFC are only available through the Android platform, but passes that are available through 1D/2D codes are available online and through the iOS app as well. However, the Wear OS version of Google Pay doesn't feature passes at all, instead only offering payment features. </p>

      <p>Those on light yellow background: originally released as Android Pay. </p>

      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a> / <a href="/wiki/Visa_Debit" title="Visa Debit">Visa Debit</a> / <a href="/wiki/Visa_Electron" title="Visa Electron">Visa electron</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Mastercard" title="Mastercard">Mastercard</a> / <a href="/wiki/Debit_Mastercard" title="Debit Mastercard">Debit Mastercard</a></li>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supported_loyalty_programs">Supported loyalty programs</span></h3>
